Caption: Nothing needs to be killed, suppressed, or purified.
Live fully. Desire. Create. Fail. Love. Lose. Rise again.
The play was never the problem — only forgetting that it is a play.

Enlightenment is not the end of the movie;
it’s simply remembering you are not the character on the screen, but the light of the projector itself.

When seeking relaxes,
when becoming ends,
when the future loses its hypnosis —
Being reveals itself as the only truth.

So the great joke is this: you have been searching for what you already are. 

The ocean has been looking for water. 
The light has been trying to see itself in a mirror. 
God has been praying to God. 

There is nothing to become — only something to stop pretending. When the mind finally drops the costume of “me,” the dance continues effortlessly, but the dancer is gone.

--- VISUAL TEXT (VLM) ---
The Upanishads state that
"Tat Tvam Asi - You are That."
Can you explain?


Everything in the world only exists because it
borrows existence from something deeper.
Imagine you are holding this cup of tea. The tea
is held by the cup - without the cup, it falls
apart. The cup is held by your hand. Remove
your hand, and the cup and tea collapse. Your
hand is supported by your arm, your arm by
your body, your body by the chair, the chair by
the floor, the floor by the Earth, the Earth by
physical forces - and so on.


So, everything in this present
moment is borrowing its ability to
exist from something more
fundamental to exist?


Exactly. Nothing in this chain has power
to exist on its own - each is upheld by
something deeper. If you remove any
level, everything above it disappears
instantly. That means, in this moment,
each layer of reality is dependent on
something before it to exist.


There must be one foundational
reality that doesn't borrow
existence, doesn't rely on anything
deeper, and simply is. This root cause
must exist right now, or nothing else
would exist; all would collapse.


Aristotle called this the 'Uncaused
Cause', Aquinas the 'Pure Actuality',
Tillich the 'Ground of All Being', and
the Upanishads call it 'Brahman.'


If everything borrows existence, there
must be an unborrowed source. That
source must be ever-present and not
dependent on anything else.That
"non-dependent ground of being" is what
classical religions mean by God.


If Brahman or God sustains all
things, where do I fit? I am just
another thing held up by that root.
Why do the Upanishads say I am
'That?'


Everything you see around you is
uphield and powered by "That" - we call
that Being itself. All forms are 'That'
appearing as shapes. But humans have
a unique capacity: we can become
aware of Being as our own nature.


And how can we do that?


God is not found by tracing a line
backward through time. Not by asking,
"What happened first?" Not by chasing a
chain of past causes. This is the causal
path of time - what science is after.


God is found by going deeper, not earlier -
into the very structure of existence right
now. Not in the beginning of the universe -
but in the Being of this very moment. God is
not the first event in a timeline.
God is the foundation beneath the timeline
Not the spark that started reality - but the
power that sustains it still.


So, you are saying the realization of
who we truly are cannot be sought in
time, using any methods? We cannot
become God - we can only be 'That',
when time ends?


Exactly. And time for us is nothing more than
thought. When we stop pondering over the
past, or imagining and seeking a future, and
instead rest in the Being of this moment - by
letting go of our egoic urge to become
something more or less - we discover a reality
that does not come or go: the source of
existence itself.


And in that discovery, we are no
longer a person searching for God. We
are the Ground on which God and the
world appear. This is the realization:
Tat Tvam Asi - You are That.


Is this why Rumi said, "Silence is
the language of God, all else is
poor translation"?


Exactly. Silence is not empty. It is
the language of the Source. Only a
jivanmukta - the living dead - one
whose ego has dissolved, who no
longer seeks, no longer remembers,
or imagines a "me" in time - can
truly hear that silence.


This is why the sages say:
You don't become God. You
stop pretending you are
anything else.


But I still desire, I still
have goals - does that
mean I am bound to never
experience 'That?'


God is the universe observing itself - and
forgetting itself to experience the game of
many. Desire is not the enemy; it is the fuel of
the game - a movement of the One exploring
its own possibilities. When the mind has
exhausted all its imagined destinations, a new
kind of seeing emerges: 'Everything I was
seeking, I already am.' God never forgot. Only
the character forgot. And when the character
remembers. there is no character left.
Only That - silent, self-existing, and free.

Type: Carousel
Caption: This post is from the last webinar on Laziness. We discussed the hidden relationship between laziness and ambition — how what we call “laziness” is often the soul’s quiet rebellion against false goals. We explored how ambition can become a collective illusion fueled by comparison and fear, and how true drive arises only when your actions are aligned with your inner truth. When effort fades and authenticity takes over, life begins to move through you — not against you.

We only know struggle, effort, force, discipline. The self-help shelves are filled with books on motivation — and for good reason. We are all alienated from our truth, trying to live a collective illusion.

Yet, there is a way. Remove everything that gives you a quick spike of pleasure — the upcoming trip, the drink after work, the smoking, the drugs, the binge eating and watching, the thrill of buying something new. Why? Because those highs keep you going. They balance the pain of living a false life.

When you remove the distractions, the pain of falsehood becomes unbearable, impossible to ignore. You will have nowhere to escape to. And when that happens, it will be impossible not to reject deception and illusion. Alignment will naturally emerge. All you need to do is create space — remove the outside noise.

A time may come after you quit the job, the fake relationships, the false roles, when you will have nothing to do. Yet, don’t fall into despair. You have created space for what is true to arise. Follow your attention. Do more of the things that naturally draw you in. It may take time, but trust the process — creative action flows from idleness, not grind. It flows from the clarity of non-doing, not the restlessness of becoming.

That was my experience. For a year or two, I did nothing at all — nothing but taking care of this body and mind. No pleasures, no effort, no false relationships. Just complete alignment with what is. And out of nowhere, the urge to write appeared. I was twenty-nine; I had never even journaled, never read a book. I simply followed my curiosity — to understand the human condition, to understand myself and this mess we have created. 

#zen#knowthyself#laziness#vedanta

--- VISUAL TEXT (VLM) ---
How can I overcome
laziness and
procrastination?


Why do you want to
overcome them?


Because I want to
achieve my goals.


When you are thirsty, do
you need motivation to
drink water?
You simply get up and
Drink.


What does that imply?


When you truly want something-when
it's real and aligned with your inner
being-there is no effort, no need for
motivation, no procrastination.
There is only movement and action.
The heart and mind act as one.


Laziness happens when there is a disconnection
between the heart and the mind.
LazINESS is not your enemy-it's a signal.
It tells you when you're off your own authentic path.
Its your soul whispering, "This is not it."
All you have to do is listen.


But why is there a disconnection
between the heart and the mind?
What does that even mean?


Since childhood, we are told that we must compete,
climb ladders, achieve, and prove our worth. The
love we receive is conditional upon conforming to
what our parents and society expect of us.
Progress, toxic productivity, achievements, and
trophies become the ways we seek love and
acceptance.


The mind, in its need to be loved, borrows
dreams-false ambitions.
It is conditioned to chase the illusion of status.
Its whispers, "No pain, no gain. Push harder, or
else you're not worthy of love."


But behind all that noise, the heart resists-because it knows.
The mind calls that resistance laziness, but for those brave
enough to listen, it's wisdom in disguise.
We are not machines.
Love is not approval.
 Love is alignment with truth-
and truth flows from the heart, not the mind.


So, the question is not how to conquer laziness, how to
be more productive, or how to achieve more.
The real question is: What does my soul truly want?
Not what you should want, not what others expect-
what you truly desire if there was absolutely nobody
on this planet.


But how do I find what I truly want-beneath
all the noise, conditioning, and false desires?
How do I know if a desire
is genuinely mine?


When you pursue something that is truly aligned with
your nature, action becomes effortless.
You don't need motivation, willpower, or discipline.
Your're no longer resisting reality-you're flowing with it,
you are in absolute harmony with what is.


And when that happens, you don't chase - you attract.
When you stop forcing effort, what is real and
effortless naturally emerges.
You are in the frequency of love and truth.
Doors open, people appear, synchroncies emerge -
not because you're striving, but because youre finally
in tune with life itself.


What if I never find my true calling?
I need money to survive-my job still
requires effort.


Then you are choosing the path of survival
and fear, not creativity and love.
You are choosing a life of dragging a stone
uphill, instead of surrendering and allowing
yourself to be carried by the river.
Effort is the mind trying to discipline the
heart, saying, "You should be doing this."
But when action comes from the heart, the
mind naturally bows and becomes its servant.


So, there's no hope for
me then?


You are exactly where you need to be.
You can't force yourself into effortlessness.
It comes naturally-through your struggles, your
pain, your own understanding. That's how you
awaken. You awaken to truth - your truth.


Let go of comparison. Realize there is no race.
There is only your path, your life, your rhythm.
An acorn does not strive to be a palm tree.
No matter how hard it tries, it will unfold into its true form.
You are no different.
Relax, trust, surrender
to the intelligence behind creation itself.

--- VISUAL TEXT (VLM) ---
What's the best meditation
technique to get enlightened?


Why do you wish to use a
technique?


Because my mind is restless,
and I want to find some peace.


Let's say I give you a breathing
technique or a posture to sit in
that makes you feel peaceful.
What would that lead to?


I would want to do that
breathing technique or sit in
that posture all the time,
because it allows me to
experience peace.


Hence, you become an
addict, a junkie.


Why did you say that?


You become an addict the moment you want to
get high and avoid the low. The low is reality, and
the high is the state you are in when you are
meditating or following a certain technique.
Like any junkie, you become addicted to your
method, because without it your mind jumps
around like an uncontrollable monkey. So you try
to keep that monkey on a leash-that's the
method. But once you go back into your life, the
leash is off, and you are back in it.


Even if the high is induced by a plant
medicine, a drug, a guru, a person, or a
method, it makes no difference because
it creates dependency. And the moment
you become dependent on your method
to get high, you are trapped.


So are you saying we should not
meditate, stop doing yoga, or
explore consciousness through
plant medicine?


The paradox is that methods do work.
But for them to work, you have to get
trapped in them first.


Once you become trapped in a method,
you begin to see that clinging to the
positive only pushes the negative away.
Liberation is not another method-it is
the absence of clinging, and the complete
acceptance and understanding of what is.
And in that moment, the method
dissolves.


Spiritual experiences have nothing to do
with enlightenment. They are about
getting high. They create and sustain the
addict who wants to avoid suffering and
cling to pleasure. Enlightenment is simply
seeing reality clearly. And from that,
spiritual experiences may naturally come
-without force, without effort.
When the flower blooms, the bees come
uninvited.


So how should we approach those
methods that give us blissful
experiences?


Observe how the moment the ego experiences
the light through a technique, it builds another
identity: the spiritual ego. The spiritual ego is the
last guardian at the gate of inner freedom.
Almost everyone will go through the phase of
feeling superior, telling others about their
experiences and methods. But one should be able
to see this clearly, without judgment, without
suppression-simply as another movement of the
ego seeking importance.


You do not want to end up a meditator or a
yogi. You want to find up free. Youwant to
find the place in yourself where awareness
and love abide. You Want to find wholeness-
that place in Yourself people call God. And
for that union to happen, all identities, all
pride, all shame must fall apart.


So go through the methods. Follow the
religious or spiritual system you are given.
But watch carefully how you slowly get
trapped. Getting trapped is precisely the
function of the method. And once you see
that the game is not about endlessly chasing
a peaceful state, but about dismantling the
very structure that makes peace conditional
- you stop. You stay still.


And that is what real freedom is.
To practice and honor your system, your
tradition, or your method- but not to
drown in it. Freedom is not the rejection
of structure, but the absence of
dependence.


If a method becomes your shelter,
You are trapped.
Sit in discipline,
act in devotion,
and abandon attachment
to every state-
high or low.
For the one who clings to peace
trembles at its loss
and turns away from the world.
The way to divinity
is not the rejection of your humanity,
but its full embrace.
Only when you sit,
not to avoid reality,
But to meet it completely,
does clarity arise.
-
The one who sees clearly
abides in The Way.
And when one abides in the Way,
the window of the soul is always open.
--
The breeze-
the experience-
may come whenever it will.
and that will not lead to bondage.

--- VISUAL TEXT (VLM) ---
How can I be peaceful when
there is so much injustice and
suffering around me?


You find peace by
uncovering peace inside you.
Peace is what you are when
you are no longer separate.


How does that even help
alleviate the suffering
around me?
That sounds selfish.


There are two paths people tend to take
when faced with this ocean of suffering.
Some close their hearts and grow numb,
becoming indifferent-not because they are
cruel, but because it feels unbearable.
Others react with anger and fight to
change things.


The path of indifference and the
path of anger both add more
suffering to the world.


When you close your heart, you
become more isolated, more separate.
In the very attempt to shield yourself,
you grow increasingly alienated, more
focused on yourself-on your fears and
pleasures. You may surround yourself
with people, yet deep down you feel
utterly alone.


Anger, too, is divisive.
It is always directed toward others-
the injustice, the wrongdoers.
Once again, you reinforce your sense
of separation by becoming righteous.
And in doing so, you suffer, because
suffering is only possible when one
feels separate, not whole.


So what is the solution,
then?


The path of consciousness and awareness.
You begin to see that any action that
arises from separation only adds more
suffering to the world. So you attend first
to the parts of yourself that make you feel
separate. You attend to your own
ignorance and to the suffering that flows
from it.


This is why healing is never only personal.
When you slow down, feel what was never
felt, and choose presence instead of
reactivity, you interrupt a long chain of
suffering. You are not fixing the world, but
you are no longer transmitting what hurts.
What you integrate within yourself no
longer needs to express itself as anger,
numbness, or harm toward others.


Then, any action that flows
from a healed heart, heals
the world.


But even if I do that, every
action I take is insignificant.
I cannot bring any real
change.


When faced with this ocean of suffering, the
worst mistake we can make is to do nothing
simply because we can only do a little.
What you do may seem small or insignificant,
yet it is the most significant thing in the world.
This is the paradox of action.


Why is no action insignificant?


At the most basic level, everything is
connected. Chemically, every atom in
your body has existed long before you-
formed in stars, carried through water,
soil, plants, and other lives. You are not a
separate entity temporarily interacting
with the world; you are the world,
temporarily arranged as you.


Because everything is interconnected, no act of
kindness is ever small. Helping a disabled person
cross the street, carrying someone's groceries,
helping an elderly person read a label, answering a
question with patience instead of irritation, offering
food to the hungry, or meeting a person facing
cancer with tenderness and care-each of these
gestures matters. You become a vehicle that
removes suffering rather than adding to it.


The way you walk, the way you listen to your wife
or your parents, the ways you read to your child, the
way you speak to a waiter-every action you take,
when done with presence and gentleness, carries
weight and touches a heart. Every act of sincere
care is like dropping a pebble into water: the ripples
move outward, quietly and endlessly, touching far
more than we will ever see.


And as consciousness deepens, you see that the
one who suffers isn't really "them" -it's you.
The boundaries blur. You realize it's all me.
From a higher perspective, you See the world as
perfect. It is the unfolding of divine law, the
evolution of souls through countless
experiences, including suffering and death.


Despite all that, the awakened heart
cries for the world, but without
despair. It acts, butwithout hatred. It
serves, but Without the illusion of
being a helper.


As Jiddu Krishnamurti said,
"You are the world and the
world is you."
Attend to your own
suffering, your own sense of
separation; heal and
transcend your
generational trauma-and
then, whatever you do, no
matter how small, becomes
a light in a world that is
profoundly dark.

dance between wanting to be and simply being.
Between the hunger to become something more
and the terrifyingly obvious truth that you are
already enough. Between chasing the next

why do you start noticing something

why does doing a favor for

People think healing is about becoming the best
version of yourself. But more often, healing is
about accepting the worst version of oneself.
Your undesirable traits, like clinginess,
anger, avoidance, formed as protective
strategies in earlier environments.


If you try to replace them with "better" traits
without understanding their function, you're
fighting a system that once kept you safe,
and that never works long-term.
Because the mind doesn't let go of a strategy
until it feels understood and safe enough to
stop protecting you.


Suppressing those "negative" traits just
creates an internal conflict. One part of you is
trying to grow, while another part is trying to
protect you from old threats.
When you accept a trait, you shift from shame to
understanding it as an outdated strategy. And
that's when you can finally change it.

Post Link: https://www.instagram.com/p/DTwvnjTiHic/
Type: Carousel
Caption: .
.

#authenticity #knowthyself #purpose #nonduality #freedomfromthemadness
--------------------
--- VISUAL TEXT (VLM) ---
How do I align with my true
nature?


To align with your true nature,
you must observe what is
natural for you. And what is.
naturalfor you is revealed by
your attention.


What do you mean by
attention? And how is it
different from concentration?


Concentration is discipline
imposed. Attention is curiosity
awakened. Concentration
belongs to the mind. Attention
belongs to the heart.


Concentration is what you are
taught in school: when energy is
forced in one direction.
It is imposed from the outside:
It chases an end result - a good
grade, approval, status, survival.


Most of us only know concentration and
effort - the suppression of the soul by the
mind that keeps repeating, "you must do
this." From that suppression, energy is
wasted; we feel exhausted and empty, so
we escape into consumption, distraction,
drugs, and entertainment.


Attention is effortless. It is the path of least
resistance. Its is the direction your being
moves when you stop pretending, when you
throw away all the 'shoulds.' It does not come
from fear - it comes from resonance. It
doesn't push - it pulls.It is the subtle gravity
of your own nature.


In Tantra, they call this Spanda - the subtle
vibration of intuition. In Hindu philosophy, they cal
it Svadharma, the law of your own being. Jung saw
this same movement as the future self manifesting
in the present, trying to guide you toward your
destiny. Different languages, different traditions, but
all pointing to the same phenomenon: the inner pull
that knows the way before you do.


But what about money,
security?


The paradox is, when you stop
trying to bend your life around
money, and instead begin to
listen - really listen - to where
your heart wants to go, a kind
of grace begins to operate.


You discover that the right people
begin to appear at the right moments.
Opportunities arrive without force,
as if placed in your path by an unseen
hand. Life begins to rearrange itself
around you because you're finally in
harmony with the divine unfolding of
your own life.


It's as if the whole universe says:
"Ah. you are finally paying attention.
You're listening now. Good. Here's the
next step." Because once you're
resting in who you truly are, God, not
as a being in the sky, but as the living
intelligence within all things takes
care of the details.


Forget the money. Acknowledge the fear but
move despite it. If your attention keeps
returning to a topic, a skill, a field, a certain
kind of work, a creative act, or even a
philosophical question, it means life is trying
to unfold something through you. Listen to
that pull. Do more of it and do less of
everything else. Allow yourself to disappear
into it completely.


Most people judge their interests.
They prematurely label what draws them as
"not useful, "not productive," "not profitable,"
and in doing so they kill their natural unfolding
in the name of practicality. Most of us don't die
when we are buried - we die the moment we
abandon what makes us alive.


Your nature doesn't yell. It doesn't force. It
doesn't require motivation or discipline. Its
doesn't threaten. It waits. It awaits for you to
stop being afraid of yourself. It waits for you too
stop needing validation. It waits for you you to trust
the intelligence of what you are
naturally drawn to.


Human beings do not create their
greatest work from safety.
They create it from truth.


Do not abandon your nature to satisfy
the world. Forget what your parents
want, what peers think is "normal," what
the culture worships, what brings status
or approval, what avoids discomfort.
This is not your nature; that is your
conditioning. It will give you a life that
looks right but feels wrong.


Allow yourself to be naturally
drawn by the divine pull of what
grabs you. Follow the thread with
curiosity. It will lead you back
home - to yourself.

Caption: Which ones (1-11) are you taking with you into 2026?

I’ve noticed a lot of the same themes coming up again and again from conversations, messages and quiet moments with people in my life.

Many aren’t confused about what they want… they’re tired of forcing it.

They’re done chasing momentum that doesn’t actually feel like theirs.

I’ve heard people question their pace because it doesn’t match what they see online.

I’ve seen people second-guess good decisions because they didn’t come with instant validation.

And I’ve watched really capable, thoughtful people carry way more than they were ever meant to carry alone.

So… this post isn’t about doing more… it’s about moving differently.

These are reminders I continue to personally move with… alignment, discernment, trust, contribution and letting go of systems that reward urgency over integrity.

Not everything meaningful needs to show up as a metric.

Not every season is meant to look impressive.

Not everything that’s right for you will feel fast.

If something in here resonates, it’s probably because you already know it… you just needed permission to honor it.

And if something feels uncomfortable, that’s information too.

Here’s to choosing your assignment in 2026.

At your pace… with integrity and coherence… and with trust in what God is already arranging.

Why do I feel lost in
life?


Feeling 'lost' isn't a problem of intelligence.
It results from an inward split. One part
of you wants truth, and another wants
approval and security. When those parts
fight, we call it "confusion."


You look outside, and what do you see?
People progressing in their careers,
starting families, buying houses, traveling,
curating spotless, happy Instagram
profiles. You look around for "landmarks,"
for signs of where you should be. You
compare your life to theirs and conclude
you're falling behind the checklist.


So you panic. You feel confused. You
start asking, "What's wrong with me?"
"Why don't I know?" "Why can't I just
choose a direction?"


Hence, our confusion is a signal: we've
let too many voices in, and we've
stopped listening to our own. We've
stopped living from the inside out and
started living for what looks right and
wins approval. We're not lost-we're just
not listening to the only voice that
matters: our heart.


Exactly. Clarity isn't a thought. It's a
state of complete radical honesty.
A state of non-deception, no pretense.
a state of truth. Direction appears
when you stop lying to yourself to
feel safe.


As you quiet down-as you release the
idea of who you should be-you begin to
hear who you actually are. And what
you hear isn't a demand to become
perfect or successful-that's
conditioning. It's an invitation to come
home, to the one place you don't have to
perform: yourself.


But how do I quiet down and find
myself after all the pressure and
conditioning?


Most people stay stuck in jobs and
relationships they hate because the
pain of misalignment feels easier
than the discomfort of facing
themselves. And there's always an
escape: drugs, good food, constant
travel, nights out, new clothes, new
plans, new distractions.


But if you remove all that-if you strip
away the noise-and you stay with
yourself when there's nothing left to
reach for,nothing left to numb the pain of
pretense, you begin to see where you
keep saying yes while your body says no;
where you perform instead of express;
WHERE you stay small to be accepted;
Where you've been living someone
else's life.


But that's scary. I may have to give
up relationships, my career, my
whole life. And then what?
What would I do next?


Think of your life like a branching
tree. At any moment, you're
standing at a node. You have two
options: you either choose truth and
self-love, or you choose fear and
self-abandonment.


If you choose fear, you stay in the
misaligned timeline. You keep what's
familiar, but you pay for it quietly: with
constant self-management-numbing,
justifying, coping, performing. You live
in survival mode. You chase. You
struggle. Life starts to feel like pushing
upstream because you're living against
your own nature.


If you choose truth, you live in the
timeline of love. Why? Because love
begins the moment you accept yourself
fully-when your heart, your actions,
and your life become one. Your energy
starts to overflow because it's no longer
wasted in inner conflict. You stop
chasing and start attracting. You Stop
forcing and start aligning.


And as you become coherent and whole,
you become magnetic. People feel the
safety of your honesty. They recognize
the steadfastness of someone who isn't
performing. Life, too, begins to respond
to your frequency-not react
to you fear.


Without planning, without force, the right
person shows up at the right time.
A conversation becomes a doorway.
An opportunity appears that you couldn't
have planned, but somehow fits perfectly.
Synchronicities arise-not because the
universe is rewarding you, but because you've
stopped fighting your own nature.


Stop comparing your path to other
people's lives. Trust the timing as divinely
set. Your only task is to keep asking this
simple question at every step:
Am I choosing love, or choosing fear?


Simple questions to ask at every step
Truth test: Is this true for me?
Body test: Does my body open or contract around this?
Integrity test: Would I still choose this if nobody ever approved of it?
Fear vs love: Am I choosing from fear ... or from love?
Energy test:Does this drain me or nourish me ?
Performance test : Is this my life -- or my performance?
Avoidance test: What feeling am I trying to avoid right now?
Alignment test: Does this require me to betray myself to keep it ?

My parents are very
unhappy with my choices.
What should I do?


Your parents are not unhappy because
you do not follow their wishes, but
because your very being and way of life
question the way they lived their lives.
You become a mirror that reflects the
ways they betrayed themselves in order to
belong and be approved.


In a way, you are not really
rejecting your parents as human
beings; you are rejecting their
conditioning and programming.


The moment you say, "I will not rush into
education, marriage, or children," you are not
merely making a personal choice-you are
shaking the foundations of the story they
told themselves in order to survive. That is
why it feels threatening. Not because you are
wrong, but because your freedom reveals
their own chains.


You need to let go of the guilt and the
pressure that you are responsible for your
parents' happiness-or anyone else's
happiness. You are not here to please, but to
discover. And discovery requires authentic
self-expression, not obedience.


But what if they are right, and I
am wrong?


Most people live their lives out of fear.
They are horrified by the responsibility of
making their own choices so they follow
scripts, suppress what feels alive in them,
and call it maturity. This suppression leads
to anger, neurosis, and resentment
later in life.

aspect of the infinite before returning to
its absolute source. There is nothing
unique in blind obedience. Life is not
meant to be a repetition, but a revelation.

courage to take responsibility for your own
unfolding, knowing that mistakes made in
honesty are far less destructive than
obedience lived in self-denial.


So the question is not whether my parents
are right or I am wrong. The real question is
whether I am willing to live truthfully-to
risk uncertainty, disappointment, and
misunderstanding-rather than betray my
own soul for the comfort of approval.

--- VISUAL TEXT (VLM) ---
The highest form of intelligence
according to neuroscience.
Part 1
@consciousness_expansion


The highest form of intelligence, according to neuroscientist
Anil Seth and psychologist Robert Sternberg, isn't logic,
speed, or memory.
It's metacognition the ability to think about your own
thinking.
Your brain literally observes itself, corrects errors, and
rewires in real time.
Every time you say, "Wait ... why did I react like that?" your
neural pathways start shifting.
That moment of self-observation is your brain evolving.


Metacognition Is the Brain Watching Itself
Neuroscientists found that when you "notice yourself
thinking", a region called the anterior prefrontal cortex
(BA10) lights up basically, the brain turns the spotlight
inward.
That means you have a neural system designed purely
for self-observation your brain studying its own code
in real time.
It's like a computer running software that edits its own
programming while running.


Self-Awareness Can Physically Rewire Your Brain
UCLA researchers discovered that simply labeling
your emotions ("I'm anxious," "I'm angry") activates
the right ventrolateral prefrontal cortex and calms the
amygdala your emotional alarm.
That means naming your inner state literally changes
brain activity awareness itself alters wiring.
It's not therapy talk it's neuroelectric remodeling.


Conscious Self-Reflection Can Rewrite Memory and
Belief
research on memory reconciliation shows that
when you recall an event while being aware you're
recalling it, your brain temporarily softens that
memory allowing new emotional meaning to
overwrite it.
That's how trauma healing and mindset rewiring
actually work:
you're not "thinking differently", you're editing your
brain's file system through awareness.

Caption: Karma isn’t about reward or punishment. It’s about evolution.
Your Sanchita is everything you’ve ever done.
Your Prarabdha is the portion you chose for this lifetime.
Your Agami is what you’re creating now.

The path was chosen by you.
But the awakening begins when you stop living as the story and start living as the witness.

[karma, sanchita karma, prarabdha karma, agami karma, vedanta, samsara, moksha, self inquiry, witness consciousness, nondual teachings, soul journey, reincarnation, spiritual evolution, inner freedom, self discovery, awareness, liberation, dharma, spiritual growth]

--- VISUAL TEXT (VLM) ---
KARMA: THE JOURNEY YOUR
SOUL CHOSE
The Architecture of Karma,
Why your life unfolds the way it does.


THINK OF YOUR SOUL AS A
TRAVELLER
Across lifetimes,
your soul journeys through thousands of
experiences,
each choice, action, intention
stored in a vast cosmic archive.
Vedanta calls this Sanchita Karma.


SANCHITA KARMA
(THE STORAGE VAULT)
Sanchita is your entire bank of Karma
accumulated across lifetimes.
Think of it as everything you've learned,
everything you've done,
every reaction, desire, and pattern,
all stored like your travel history.


HOW PRARABDHA KARMA IS
CHOSEN
Before each life,
your soul chooses a small portion of the Sanchita
to work through in the next lifetime,
much like deciding which part of the world you
want to explore next.
This chosen portion becomes the itinerary
for the life ahead.


WHAT PRARABDHA KARMA
DETERMINES
It includes the events you must experience to
evolve ... family, body, major turning points,
joys, losses, opportunities, lessons.
This part cannot be changed.
It is what you came here to live.


KRIYAMANA / AGAMI KARMA
(HOW YOU TRAVEL)
But how you walk your path,
your responses, awareness, reactions, choices,
create new Karma.
Two people may have the same itinerary
but live completely different journeys ...
based on the way they respond.
This is Agami Karma,
what you accumulate now for the future.


THE DANCE OF KARMA
At any moment in your life,
three forces are at play:
· Sanchita: everything stored
· Prarabdha: what you chose to work through
now
· Agami: What you are creating through your
responses
This is the machinery of evolution.


SAMSARA (THE LOOP)
Sanchita > Prarabdha > Agami > back to Sanchita.
Lifetime after lifetime.
Birth after birth.
Experience after experience.
This is Samsara,
the cycle of becoming.
The loop continues
as long as identification continues.


THE WAY OUT
(THE VEDANTIC SHIFT)
The way out is not changing the itinerary.
It is changing your identity within it.
Liberation begins when you ...
stop living as the body, role, personality, or story,
and begin living as there witness of all experience.
When you see life as a traveller, not the trip.
 When you seek the Self beneath all layers,
beyond name, form, desire, fear.
This is the inward turning.
The moment awareness wakes up to itself.


MOKSHA (FREEDOM WHILE
LIVING)
Moksha is not escape.
It is recognition.
Recognizing that you are not the itinerary,
not the experience,
Not the story,
but the witness in which the entire journey unfolds.
When the witness awakens,
Karma loses its bondage.
The cycle dissolves.


Your life is not random.
You chose the lessons you are learning.
And you choose every moment
how you walk them.
Understand Karma,
and your life becomes less of a struggle
and more of a journey toward yourself.

Caption: Quantum physics shows that observation influences reality.
Vedanta says awareness is the field in which reality appears.

Both point to a single mystery:
consciousness is not inside the universe,
the universe appears inside consciousness.

The observer is not the person.
It is the presence behind the person.
And when you discover that witness within you,
you begin to see the world
not as something separate,
but as something arising in awareness itself. ✨

[consciousness, observer effect, quantum mechanics, Vedanta, Purusha, Sakshi, Maya, unified field, Upanishads, wavefunction collapse, awareness, nonduality, physics and spirituality]
--------------------
--- VISUAL TEXT (VLM) ---
THE OBSERVER AND REALITY
We use the word "observer" all the time.
Science and Vedanta both point to
something deeper.
Reality is never entirely "out there."
It depends on how it is seen.


THE OBSERVER IN QUANTUM
PHYSICS
At the heart of quantum mechanics sits a mystery:
observation changes what's observed.
In the double-slit experiment:
· particles behave like waves,
· until measured,
then they "collapse" into one state.
Meaning: The act of observing alters reality.
Not consciously,
but fundamentally.


WHAT PHYSICISTS AGREE ON
Quantum mechanics does not claim that
consciousness collapses the wave.
But it does say:
A particle remains in superposition, until a
measurement or interaction happens ... then it
becomes "something definite."
The real question remains unresolved.
What counts as an observer?
And why does observation change reality at all?


THE OBSERVER IN VEDANTA
Vedanta has its own language:
· Sakshi, the witness, the silent awareness behind
experience
· Purusha, pure consciousness, distinct from
Prakriti
· Brahman, the field of awareness in which all
phenomena appear
Here, the observer is not the mind,
it is the field in which the mind appears.


A SHARED MYSTERY
Quantum physics says:
Reality exists as probabilities
until an observation occurs.
Vedanta says;
The world is Maya,
an appearance that exists
only in relation to the observer or witness,
ie. Sakshi.
Both traditions point to the same truth:
Realty is not fully independent of the one who
sees it.


UNIFIED FIELD
(TWO PERSPECTIVES)
Physics calls it:
A unified field of energy.
Vedanta calls it;
Pure consciousness (Brahman).
Science studies the field as forces and particles.
 Vedanta studies it as awareness itself.
Different languages ...
Same direction:
everything arises from one underlying essence.


SO WHAT IS THE OBSERVER?
Not the brain.
No the eyes.
NOT the ego.
Not even the thoughts.
The observer is the non-objective presence
in which reality becomes experience,
whether through measurement in physics
or awareness in Vedanta.
It is the "space" ...
inwhich potential becomes real.


THE VEDANTIC PARALLEL
Vedanta says:
You are not in the universe.
The universe is in consciousness.
-
The observer is not separate from what is observed.
Both arise within the same field of awareness.
--
The Upanishads call Consciousness Brahman,
and that same Consciousness,
when experienced within us,
is the Sakshi, the silent witness.


IMPORTANT CAUTION
Quantum mechanics is science.
Vedanta is spirituality.
Their parallels are profound,
but metaphorical, not literal.
Yet both help us see that:
reality is not solid,
not fixed ,
not independent.
It is relational.
Dynamic.
Interconnected.


Between physics and philosophy
a single truth emerges:
The observer is not separate from the world.
The Observer brings the world into experience.
In science: through measurement.
In spirituality: through awareness.
IN both: through presence.
And this presence
is the deepest layer of who you are.

Post Link: https://www.instagram.com/p/DQ_oxxjkqxR/
Type: Carousel
Caption: How to kill emotions and rewire yourself - Enjoy.
--------------------
--- VISUAL TEXT (VLM) ---
How To Kill Emotions.


Turning off Emotions
Without Self-Sabotage
When people feel emotional,
they instinctively turn to what's made them
feel better in the past.
For most, that means food, alcohol,
cigarettes - anything to numb the emotion.
I've done that too.
But I needed something that wouldn't ruin my
health or derail my goals.
So I built a framework:
something I could actually rely on when
things got rough.
It's simple, easy to implement,
and has helped me have zero emotion where
most people collapse.
Here's the 4-step process I use to handle
frustration before it ruins my day:


Step 1: Acknowledge the Thought
The first move is to stop, pause, and identify
the exact thought that's creating the distress.
We talk to ourselves at about 4,000 words
per minute - that's faster than a machine
gun, which means it's easy to get swept away
without realising what's happening.
Emotional engagement clouds clarity.
You need to cut through the noise.
Ask yourself:
1. What's the thought?
Open your notes app.
Write it down.
Let it spill without editing or trying to sound
smart.
Just get it all out. Then ask:
2. What are you scared of?
Be honest.
Say the quiet part out loud - even if it chokes
you up.
That sentence will reveal the core fear behind
the clutter.


Fake fears
Insecurities
Core
Most of what rises first is noise,
ego-protection and surface-level fear.
But the second question digs to the real
issue. And that's what gives you power:
naming the actual problem.


Step 2: Diffuse from the Emotion
Now that you've identified the thought,
you need to separate from it
not suppress it, not argue with it
- just create space.
This is called diffusion.
You're stepping back and observing your
thought instead of being consumed by it.
Two visual techniques that help:


1. Fish in a Pond
Visualise your thoughts as fish in a pond.
Most are calm, peaceful.
But there's one rotten fish - the one making
you miserable.
Don't touch it. Just observe it.
Tell yourself: "This thought is not me. It's just
something floating by."
That distance is everything.
2. Books on a Shelf
You're in a library, surrounded by books.
One of those books is fear.
You can pick it up, even glance at it. The
But you don't have to read it. You can put it back and choose something
more useful.
Once you notice the thought as separate
from you, the emotional charge starts to
fade.


Step 3: Accept the Thought
Here's what most people get wrong:
Once they've named the thought and seen it
clearly, they want it gone.
But it doesn't go.
So instead of fighting it, accept it.
Ask yourself:
"If this thought never went away ... what
would I do?"
Answer: you'd live your life anyway.
You carry it. Like a photo in your wallet.
you don't stare at it all day.
Your don't forget it exists.
BUT you also don't obsess over it. "
That's real acceptance.
Not loving the thought, but not needing it to
vanish.
And the more irrational your emotional
response feels, the more likely it's been
shaped by the belief system (BS) you've
absorbed over time.


Step 4: Reorient Toward Your
Goal
You can't think your way out of a thinking
problem.
You need to act your wayout.
Steps 1-3 buy you space.
Stop 4 gets you moving again.
Ask yourself:
"What action can I take right now that
moves me closer to my goals?"
Write it down. Then do it.
This is how you reclaim influence over your
outcomes. Not by wishing away bad feelings,
but by choosing a better response than the
one your emotions are pushing you toward.
"I'm the one doing the responding.
 This is on me."
That truth stings.
But it's the only way forward.
This is How you get better, and stay better,
without spiralling into coping behaviour.


7 Habits That Will Sharpen
Your Mind, Body, and Life
These aren't cute slogans or vague life
advice. These are habits that build resilience,
consistency, clarity, and control.
Pick them up - and watch your trajectory
change.


1. Waste Time - But Do It
Consciously
Everyone wastes time. Even billionaires.
The difference is whether you do it
deliberately or let it control you.
When you choose how to "waste" time - it's
no longer waste.
It's recovery. It's management. Its control.
Use short-term rewards to reinforce progress.
I complete a task > I take myself to a
cafe
· I complete another > I eat a steak
Task > Reward > Repeat
The real waste? Spending hours with people
who add nothing to your life.
That's not recharging - that's regression.


2. Keep Moving
Stay in motion - mentally and physically.
Stagnation is where overthinking starts.
When you stop moving, your mind spirals. It
invents problems. It gets loud.
Constant motion keeps your emotional
circuitry busy.
Not distracted - engaged.
This doesn't mean avoid rest.
It means avoid idleness.
3. Do Something Physically Brutal
First Thing in the Morning
I do max pull-ups straight out of bed. No
warmup. No stretching. Just effort.
Why?
It kicks my adrenaline into gear
It makes everything else that day feel
easy by comparison
It builds resilience, consistency, and pain
tolerance - daily
Anyone can work hard at 4pm.
Doing something painful when you're half-
asleep? That rewires your identity.


4. Only 3 Things Matter Daily
You get 3 priorities. That's it.
Everything else? Distraction. Noise. Wasted
bandwidth.
Pick 3 things that move your life forward
health
income
skill acquisition
and build your entire day around them.
Not 10. Not 5. Three.


5. Ditch Vague Goals
"Be happy,"
"Feel emotionally stable."
"Get more confident."
None of that counts.
If it isn't tangible or measurable, it isn't real.
It's filler.
Its a feel-good slogan with no structure.
Real goals look like:
Earn X by Y
Help 20 clients reach X milestone
Run a 5K in under 25 minutes
Read 12 books this year
Goals need math. Trackable inputs. Clear
outcomes.


6. Live by Non-Negotiables
Set standards for yourself that don't
fluctuate with mood, weather, or motivation:
Train consistently. Doesn't have to be
weightlifting, but it must be hard,
progressive, and structured.
Track calories/macros. Even if you're
not chasing abs, knowing your intake
gives you leverage over your body
composition at any time.
Consume quality info daily. Books,
research, articles - keep sharpening
your lens.
Do math regularly. Keeps binary logic
sharp. Yes, basic arithmetic counts.
Get medical data. No "faguzi!" No
pseudo-healing. Run full-body labs at
least twice a year. Know what's
happening inside. Don't guess.
Standards over feelings - always.


7. Do It Now
If it takes under 5 minutes, do it immediately.
Make this a personal policy. No exceptions.
It starts small - like washing dishes right
after eating - but it compounds.
That one habit kills procrastination, builds
trust in your own follow-through, and speeds
up every area of life.
Never leave "dirty dishes" - literal or
metaphorical.


Bonus: How I See the Stimulus-
Response Cycle Now
I used to think:
Stimulus > Response > Outcome
Simple, direct, clean.
But that's not how real frustration works.
Now I understand it like this:
S>T>F>U>R>O
S= Stimulus
What's frustrating you? Who or what's in
your way?
T = Thoughts
What are you telling yourself about this?
What meaning are you assigning?
F= Feelings
What emotions are those thoughts
creating?
U = Urge
What impulse do those feelings push you
toward?
Is it constructive or destructive?
R = Response
What do you actually choose to do?
O = Outcome.


So if you're frustrated,
remember to STFU.

Caption: Maya is not just distraction or attachment.
It is the entire field of experience: senses, thoughts, memories, desires, fears, comparisons, identity, every thread in your perception.

Vedanta and quantum mechanics both point to the same insight.
The world you see is shaped by the one who sees it.

The more you search outside, the deeper you sink into Maya.
The moment you turn inward, the illusion begins to thin.

The sages never told you to escape life.
They told you to wake up within it. ✨

YOU'RE NOT SEEING REALITY.
YOUR'RE SEEING MAYA.
Most people think Maya is
attachment or material illusion.

Maya is the entire appearance of reality.

Vedanta has always said reality is projected,
not perceived.

A self evolving illusion that keeps Consciousness
engaged.

Maya is not deception.
It is the mechanism of manifestation itself.
The cosmic interface that lets the infinite appear as
the finite.
Everything you see, hear, touch, feel, desire, fear,
or remember ... arises through Maya.


WHY YOU GET CAUGHT IN IT
The more you identify with the senses, with
achievements, status, desires, comparison,
the deeper you fall into the simulation.
Maya adapts to your mind.

like an algorithm learning your patterns.

OUTSMART

-

The losses feel real

Brahma satyam jagat mithya
jivo brahmaiva naparah
Adi Shankaracharya
Brahim, the Absolute, alone is real.
The world is an appearance. The individual self is nothing but Brahman.
Maya is the appearance.
You are the Reality behind it.


You don't escape Maya by abandoning the world.
You escape it by seeing through it.
Once you see it,
the illusion becomes light;
the world becomes play,

the universe is not outside you.
It arises within you ..

Caption: Extreme ambition that is accompanied by unhealthy tension and (mostly self-imposed) pressure usually comes from a previously experienced feeling of inferiority.

This doesn’t mean you need to abandon your ambition. This is one of the things depth psychology, existential psychology, and humanistic psychology have in common: It’s not about “fixing” you and removing the supposedly problematic parts of you.

They recognize mental health as a creative project. The tensions inside of you are to be adjusted and readjusted so that the person moves towards integration. Because integration is the defining characteristic of mental health, not perfect equilibrium.

Caption: Tara had just left Khajuraho, still carrying the memory of stone bodies carved in embrace.

And now, the Himalayas awaited 
the land of goddesses and her ancestors, 
where silence feels like a meditation itself.

The car curved through the giant mountains of Himachal, 
rain pouring across the windshield.

Outside, monkeys jumped around 
wanting to steal another banana and bread 
from the locals.

Inside the car, Tara stared out of the window, 
feeling unsettled. 

In the vastness of the mountains and the journey, 
her mother’s voice followed her.

“What’s gotten into you, Tara?
A woman needs a secure home.
You’re throwing away everything...
your marriage, your respect, your safety.

Adam will find someone else. 

Men always do.

But for women… people never forget.
You can still go back, you can still fix this.”

Her mother’s words echoed louder 
than the Bollywood music the driver was playing.

Tara closed her eyes.

She realized she might be physically in India,
but emotionally, she was still in that New York apartment,
still negotiating between her freedom and her conditioning.

The road turned sharper.

She inhaled the scent of wet earth 
— grounding, ancient, unflinching.

As the car stopped before the steps of the Goddess Chamunda Temple,
she stepped out, barefoot, the mud cool beneath her feet.

The bells rang again, distant but calling.
And there, standing before the goddess, 
she finally understood.

Home was never the apartment Adam paid for.

Home was not the promise of security, 
or the approval of her mother’s trembling fear.

Home was her body.
Her breath.
Her land.
Her truth.

Because if you build your life 
on someone else’s ground,
they will always decide how high 
your walls can rise.

To live freely, 
you must claim your own soil 
even if it means walking alone.

She whispered to herself,
“This isn’t confusion. This is remembering my roots.”

As she looked up, the clouds parted.
A shaft of light touched her face,
and for the first time, she didn’t flinch a bit.
She smiled 
because she found 
the home 
that never left her.

Post Link: https://www.instagram.com/p/DQ_ru64jdXn/
Type: Carousel
Caption: Ever noticed how the moment you choose something… a little fear shows up quietly?

You love someone → suddenly there’s fear of losing them.
You feel joy → a part of you worries when the next low will come.
You make a big life decision → and instantly regret or FOMO creeps in.

For the longest time, even I didn’t understand why this happens.
But the more I worked with clients, and the more I explored Advaita & inner work, the answer became clear:

Suffering begins in the exact moment we take a position.
When we call something “good,” everything that doesn’t match it becomes “bad.”

When we choose light, we start fearing darkness.
When we choose joy, we fear losing it.
When we call something right, the opposite becomes wrong.

It’s not the situation that hurts us.
It’s our attachment to one side of the coin that creates fear of the other.

And here’s the healing part… Darkness isn’t real.
It’s just the space where your awareness hasn’t entered yet.

Sadness is the place where joy hasn’t been recognized.
Your blocks are simply forgotten corners of your own light.

When you begin to see this,
life stops feeling like a game of “either/or.”

You don’t cling. You don’t resist.
You begin to walk the middle path -where peace doesn’t depend on circumstances…it comes from awareness.

If you’re feeling stuck between choices, or if you’re constantly swinging between extremes in life or emotions,this is usually the loop of Duality & Maya.

And awareness is the first door out of it.

and we’ll start your journey into clarity, alignment and inner truth.

everything, and you're wise enough to
know none of will matter in 100 years.


As bizarre as it sounds, I think
that might be where peace lives.


In the strange liminal space between
self-importance and cosmic indifference.
Between control and chaos. Obsession
and perspective. Between going all in
and letting it all go. That's the art of life.


Because life's too short not to
make a dent while you're here.


But also ... lighten the fuck up. Laugh
at yourself. None of us really know
what we're doing. We're just slightly
evolved apes on a spinning rock,
trying to make it mean something.

Caption: We’re so addicted to speed that we’ve forgotten how to witness a person slowly. How to observe rather than imagine. Most ppl think getting to know someone means asking questions, sharing stories, or spending time.

Not by asking who they want to be, but by watching how they handle boredom, disappointment, boundaries. Not by listening to their love language, but by observing how they treat themselves when no one is affirming them.

--- VISUAL TEXT (VLM) ---
A Japanese psychologist:
smart decisions only
appear when the brain
stops "trying to be
smart" (it sounds like a
paradox but it's a fact):
@mirimika_art


1. When you try to sound intelligent the
brain switches into "defense mode." The
prefrontal cortex, the part responsible for
control, starts censoring every thought.
In that moment creative areas literally shut
down. Neuroscientists call this the cognitive
choke: the harder you Try to appear
competent the fewer ideas you produce.
That's why your best insights come in the
shower, not in a meeting.
@mirimika_art


2. A researcher in Kyoto asked students
to solve problems under time pressure.
Those who "tried to think smart" made
more mistakes than those who
responded quickly and intuitively.
EEG scans showed that during "effortful
thinking," activity in the parietal lobes, the
parts that integrate information, dropped
sharply
The attempt to impress literally breaks the
neural network.
@mirimika_art


3. People obsessed with being right
suffer from a constant audience effect
even when alone.
They mentally grade every phrase as if
someone's watching. This suppresses
dopamine, the chemical that fuels
insight. One Tokyo psychologist said,
"When you try to be smart, you stop
being alive."
That's the paradox: intelligence grows
not from effort but from relaxed attention.
@mirimika_art


4. The only way to fix it is to remove control.
Don't force yourself to think, allow your brain to
wander.
Scientists call this the default mode network:
when attention drifts, neurons start connecting
unpredictably, generating insights.
That's why the best ideas come while you're
washing dishes, riding the subway, or staring
at a wall.
@mirimika_art


5. To regain speed and clarity of thought, stop
pushing your intellect. Write the problem down,
close the laptop, and do something physical
like cleaning, walking, or showering.
When control loosens, the brain delivers the
answer on its own. Intelligence isn't tension, it's
the skill of releasing.
Have you noticed that the sharpest answers
usually come right after you stop looking for
them?
@mirimika_art


Subscribe to my free newsletter for more
insights.
Would love to see you in our warm circle <3
Link in bio
@mirimika_art

Post Link: https://www.instagram.com/p/DQtrwoSCB-0/
Type: Carousel
Caption: There are many similarities in how both men and women regulate their nervous systems, but there are also some important differences.

The main difference is this:

Men’s nervous systems are predominantly dopamine-based.
Women’s nervous systems are predominantly oxytocin-based.

Men thrive on purpose. Women thrive on connection.

Now, before anyone comments: yes, men also need connection, and women also need purpose—that’s why I intentionally used the term “#1 regulator.”

A man’s nervous system is wired more transactionally:
„I do good—therefore I feel good.“

A woman’s nervous system is wired more relationally:
„I feel good—therefore I do good.“

That’s why women suffer in an overly-masculine society that values productivity over connection. Even the “spiritual boss babe” runs on that dopamine-high.

It’s also why “spiritual” men suffer. Walking a overly-relational feminine path as a man can erode your sense of agency—and leave you stuck in what I call spiritual depression.

Understanding and honouring this ancient biological truth is paramount. It allows us to work with our biology instead of against it.

Ardently ❤️‍🔥
Felix

#nervoussystemregulation

Type: Carousel
Caption: A SCIENTIST PROVED TIME IS FAKE AND REALITY BENDS TO THOUGHT. THE CIA CLASSIFIED IT FOR 26 YEARS. PAGE 25 REVEALED: “CONSCIOUSNESS CAN REWRITE THE PAST.” THEN HE DIED IN FLIGHT 191.
In 1977, Itzhak Bentov—a biomedical engineer with NASA connections and multiple patents—sat down with the CIA.
His theory: The universe isn’t “out there.” It’s a hologram inside you. Time is an illusion. Reality bends to focused thought.
The CIA took him seriously.
They created a classified 29-page report: “Analysis and Assessment of Gateway Process.”
Conclusion: “Human consciousness can access any point in time. There is no past or future—only NOW.”
Page 25 went missing for 26 years.
When declassified in 2003, it revealed:

“Time is a construct of the conscious mind”
“Consciousness can collapse quantum probabilities”
“Reality can be edited through focused intention”

Bentov’s method:
Enter theta state → Synchronize brain hemispheres → Apply focused intention
Result? Reshape memory, influence probability, access information beyond space-time.
NASA used his techniques. The Pentagon reportedly feared it.
May 25, 1979:
Bentov boarded Flight 191 to present his research in Japan. The engine detached. 271 dead. His files lost.
One line survived: “We are energy experiencing frequency projected into form.”
What’s verified:
✓ Real inventor (NASA, patents)
✓ CIA document is declassified
✓ Page 25 missing for 26 years
✓ Died in Flight 191 (maintenance failure)
What’s theoretical:
? Consciousness rewriting timelines
? Reality manipulation through thought

WHAT IF DETACHMENT ISN'T

THE REAL MEANING OF DETACHMENT
People think detachment means
forgetting everyone, walking away, or
becoming emotionless.
But that's not detachment - that's
avoidance.
True detachment isn't cold or distant.
It's the art of staying peaceful even while
you're deeply connected to others.


Shiva never ran from love.
He lived in it - consciously.
 He didn't detach from Parvati;
he detached from expectation.
His peace didn't depend on her presence
- it came from within.
That's spiritual maturity, not indifference.


What Detachment Really Means?
Detachment means you still care,
but you don't cling.
You love fully,
But you dont lose yourself.
you give without expecting anything back.
It's about controlling your mind,
not your emotions.


When someone doesn't reply or
disappoints you -
don't react with anger or insecurity.
Instead, breathe.
Remind yourself: love is about giving, not
controlling.
When you stop expecting,
you start loving in peace - not pressure.


Parvati meditated for years to unite
with Shiva.
He never forced her return ..
He didn't chase, yet he never stopped
loving.
That's divine trust -
a connection that doesn't need
constant proof or control to exist.


We mistake attachment for love.
We crave replies, attention, validation.
WE call obsession "care."
But that's not love - it's dependency
wearing a sweet mask.
Love shouldn't make you anxious;
it should make you aware.


When you stop expecting,
you stop suffering.
You don't stop caring -
you start seeing love clearly, without
conditions or fear.
That's what Shiva practiced:
Love as freedom, not as possession.


It's not about leaving people behind.
It's about remembering yourself within
love.
You can be loyal, emotional, kind -
and still detached.
Because detachment isn't
disconnection;
it's emotional strength disguised as
peace.


Shiva teaches us:

but never lose your balance.

loving without expectation.

--- VISUAL TEXT (VLM) ---
THE FIVE ILLUSIONS THAT
KEEP YOU FROM KNOWING
WHO YOU TRULY ARE
Vedanta's Map to Strip Away the False Self.


The First Question
the Upanishads Ask
"Who am I?" this is not a casual question
in Vedanta. It is the primal inquiry (atma-
vicara) upon which the entire pursuit of
Self-realization rests.
Most of us answer it with roles: I am a
daughter, a friend, an entrepreneur, a
seeker. Some go deeper. I am my
emotions, my memories, my story. But
Vedanta says: peel all this away, and
you'll find that none of it touches your
real essence.


Layer One: The Physical
Sheath (Annamaya Kösa)
The body is our most obvious identity.
We spend decades sculpting, feeding,
adorning, and protecting it. Yet Vedanta
reminds us, it is "made of food" (anna),
and one day returns to the same five
elements.
You are not this body, because you can
observe it aging, moving, and changing.
What you can observe cannot be your
ultimate Self.


Layer Two: The Energy
Sheath (Prānamaya Kosá)
Beneath the body runs the subtle current
of prāna, life force. Breath, circulation,
vitality, without which the body collapses.
But here too, Vedanta asks: are you the
breath, or the one who notices "I am
breathing"? If you can witness it, you are
beyond it.


Layer Three: The Mental
Sheath (Manomaya Kosa)
Here live your thoughts, feelings, and
endless chatter. I like, I dislike, I fear, I
desire. This sheath creates the personality
mask through which you interact with the
world.
Yet even the mind is not you, because
every night in deep sleep, thoughts
disappear, yet you do not. Something
remains, silently present.


Layer Four: The Intellectual
Sheath (Vijñanamaya Kosa)
This is the faculty of discrimination,
reasoning, and ego. I know, I choose,
I am this person. It is subtler than
emotion, but still, Vedanta declares:
even intellect is observed.
It rises in waking, fades in dream,
vanishes in deep sleep. Thus, you
cannot be reduced to mere intellect.


Layer Five: The Bliss Sheath
(Anandamaya Kosa)
The most subtle layer, felt as peace, joy, or
fulfillment, especially in deep sleep or
meditation. Yet Vedanta warns: even this is
a sheath. Why? Because it comes and goes.
The bliss of sleep ends when you wake. The
joy of meditation fades when the mind stirs.
True Self is not an experience that appears
and disappears. It is the unchanging
witness behind all experiences.


Beyond the Sheaths:
The Real You (Atman)
When the Upanishads peel away these five
coverings (pañca kosá), what remains is the
Self, sat-cit-ánanda: pure existence, pure
consciousness, pure bliss.
Not the body, not the mind, not even fleeting
bliss, but the very awareness that illuminines
them all.
This Self is:
· Unborn and deathless
· Unchanging amidst change
· Infinite, invisible, untouched by sorrow


Why Does This Matter?
Because as long as you identify with the
layers, you live in fear, of aging, loss,
failure, rejection. But when you recognize
the Self, fear falls away.
Vedanta does not ask you to become
something new. It asks you to stop
confusing yourself with the non-Self.
Liberation is not an achievement, it is a
recognition of what you always already are.


A Contemplation to Begin
Sit quietly and ask:
· Am I the body? If yes, then who is aware
of the body ?
.
Am I the mind? If yes , then who notices
the rise and fall of thoughts?
. Am I bliss? If ye, then why does it vanish
in time?
Peel back, layer by layer. What remains
when nothing else can be stripped away?
That is who you are.
Vedanta doesn't give you a new identity. It
removes all that you are not, until only the
Real remains.

Post Link: https://www.instagram.com/p/DPGbuD9Edep/
Type: Carousel
Caption: Vigyan Bhairav Tantra - The Science of Stillness

The Vigyan Bhairav Tantra is not a scripture about worshipping an external God - it is a revelation of God as a state of pure stillness. This state is Turiya - the fourth, the silent awareness beyond waking, dreaming, and deep sleep. It is the source of all creation, the Unmanifested, resting in itself as infinite consciousness. 🌌

Here, Bhairava is not a deity outside but the very ground of your being - the formless Absolute, pulsing silently within every breath, every moment. The Tantra declares that when the restless mind subsides, and you enter deep stillness, the truth of divinity is directly realized.

What makes this text unique is its practicality. The Vigyan Bhairav Tantra offers 112 methods of self-realization, each a doorway into absolute consciousness. From focusing on breath, sound, or silence - to gazing into the void, to resting in awareness of the present - these are not philosophies but living techniques to dissolve illusion and taste the eternal.

The essence is simple: God is not outside you. God is your stillness. When you rest in silence, without clinging to thought or form, Bhairava reveals Himself as your own true Self - boundless, radiant, unborn.

Aum Namah Shivaya 🕉️🔥
#VigyanBhairavTantra #Turiya #Bhairava #Stillness #ShivaConsciousness #SpiritualAwakening #TheThirdHighExperience

VIGYAN BHAIRAV TANTRA:
112 Doors to Awakening
The Ultimate Consciousness Hack
What if enlightenment was hidden in your next breath?
112 precise techniques. No philosophy. Pure experiment

Shiva's response?
Not mystical poetry. 112 DOORWAYS.
· Each technique = one pathway home.
The divine conversation that changed
everything.

· Your breath

112 methods for every consciousness type:

WORLD EMBRACERS
Sight, sound, touch practices
No matter how your awareness works,

Technique #1 -
The Breath Gap Portal
"In the natural pause after exhale and before
inhale, rest there."
THE FOUNDATIONAL PRACTICE:
.
Breathe naturally (don't control)
Notice the gap after you exhale
Rest your attention in that stillness
· Don't force anything
That gap = direct portal to pure
consciousness.
Try it right now. Seriously.
Feel the pause. Rest there.


Technique #2 - Feel the Feeler
"When any sensation arises, turn attention to
the one feeling it."
The Awareness Flip:
When you experience:
· Pleasure/Pain
· Hot/Cold
· Happy/Sad
Don't analyze the feeling.
FIND THE FEELER.
This shifts you from:
. Experience > EXPERIENCER
· Object > SUBJECT
You are not the feeling
O
O+ You are the awareness in which feeling
appears.


Technique #3 -
The Inner Sound Current
"Listen to the sound of flowing water, or AUM,
until it dissolves into silence."
THE SOUND PORTAL:
Sit quietly, eyes closed
Listen to any constant sound (fan, traffic,
silence itself)
Go deeper into the listening
Notice the sound behind the sound
Let even that dissolve
Discovery:
. You are the silence in which all sounds
appear and disappear.
The inner sound = your direct line to the
absolute.


The Ultimate Goal - Samadhi

To shatter the illusion of separation.

that:
. The meditator
.
The meditation
· The object
FUSE INTO ONE = SAMADHI

You realize you ARE what you were seeking.

--- VISUAL TEXT (VLM) ---
Paradoxically, becoming a truly "good"
person means admitting you're also capable
of bad: selfishness, jealousy, even harm.
Human beings aren't simply good or bad.
We're complex, and psychology shows we all
carry a shadow: parts of ourselves we deny,
repress, or project onto others.


When we refuse to acknowledge these
aspects, they don't disappear; they often
show up unconsciously in our relationships
and behaviors.
People with a nuanced and realistic self-
concept tend to be more compassionate and
grounded than those who cling to an idealized
image of themselves.


True goodness isn't found in denying our
darker impulses but in consciously
integrating them.
Accepting our complexity allows us to take
responsibility, cultivate empathy, and live with
greater integrity.

The 5 Types of Wealth


The Luck Razor
When choosing between two paths, choose the path
that has a larger luck surface area. Your actions put
you in a position where luck is more likely to strike.
It's hard to get lucky watching TV at home-it's easy
to get lucky when you're engaging and learning.
@Sahil Bloom
The 5 Types of Wealth


The Feynman Razor
If you can't explain it to a 5-year-old, you don't
really understand it. Complexity and jargon are used
to mask a lack of deep understanding. If someone
uses a lot of complexity and jargon to explain
something, they probably don't understand it
@Sahil Bloom
The 5 Types of Wealth

Occam's Razor
When you're weighing alternative explanations

assumptions should be chosen. Put simply,
the simplest explanation is often the best one.
Simple Assumptions> Complex Assumptions.

never take advice from people on the sidelines.

Post Link: https://www.instagram.com/p/DMqAFRIskBK/
Type: Carousel

--- VISUAL TEXT (VLM) ---
There is significant multidisciplinary evidence
suggesting that future states have more influence
on the present than does the past
Here's a summary of 5 of those takes
and their implications for what it means for
you to go from unconscious to conscious
and become the predominant creator of your reality


The Central Premise
Most systems, including human consciousness,
are organized around reducing surprise (or
uncertainty). This means that behavior,
perception, and emotional states in the present
are not purely responses to the past, but are
actively shaped by the future states the system
predictly or imagines.
If you let past experiences define your
predictions, you unconsciously create
future states that mirror your past, and
your present body-mind organizes itself in
anticipation of that repeated reality.
. If you consciously choose a different future
attractor, you can reorganize your present
state in alignment with what you want rather
than what you've experienced before.


1. Psychology and Neuroscience: The Predictive
Brain
Predictive Processing & Active Inference
(Karl Friston): The brain doesn't passively
react to stimuli but generates predictions of
the future and acts to confirm or minimize
errors in these predictions.
When your future predictions are
unconsciously shaped by the past, you stay
trapped in the same loop of reactions and
states.
o For example:
Past trauma > future expectation
of danger > present anxiety (even
in safe moments).
Conscious creation involves updating the
predictive model to a desired future,
allowing the brain and body to "pre-live" that
future state now.
This suggests that your experience of the
present is downstream from your future
predictions more than from your past events.
The past only matters insofar as it seeds your
model of what's coming.


2. Systems Thinking and Complex Systems
Attractor States: In dynamic systems,
behavior is often organized around
attractors, described as stable states the
system tends toward.
Your future goals, intentions, or imagined
states can act as attractors that shape
present action and even internal states.
Robert Fritz's structural tension theory
explicitly states:
When a system holds a vivid
image of a desired future and
a clear sense of the present
reality, the tension between
the two naturally generates
action that resolves the gap.
· A person living unconsciously will let old
attractions (past trauma, cultural
conditioning) dominate their present
structure.
But if you consciously create new future
attractor, the system self-organizes
around that new future, influencing how you
feel and act right now.


3. Physics and Retrocausality
In certain interpretations of quantum
mechanics (e.g ., Aharonov's Two-State
Vector Formalism or John Cramer's
Transactional Interpretation), future
boundary conditions can influence present
quantum states.
This doesn't mean time runs backward, but
that the future and past jointly determine
the present and reality emerges from both
initial and final conditions.
While this is still speculative, it aligns with the
idea that future states have causal
influence on the present just as the past
does, like a beautiful symmetry of influence
across time.


4. The Psychological Experience of Future
Influence
When you imagine a future outcome, your
nervous system doesn't treat it as neutral.
· Visualization studies show that rehearsing a
positive future (e.g ., athletes imagining
successful performance) primes the
nervous system as if it is already living that
outcome.
Conversely, when you expect failure
(because your past predicts it), your body
will manifest the physiological state of
failure now. This is living unconsciously.
Your body reacts to the future state you are
holding, whether that future is unconsciously
projected from the past or consciously created by
choice.


5. Conscious vs. Unconscious Creation
· Unconscious Living:
o Past > Predictions > Future state
projected > Present body-mind
becomes that state (anxiety, fear,
stagnation).
· Conscious Creation:
Chosen Future > Present alignment
(emotion, posture, mindset) > Actions >
Future actualized.
The critical shift is who is in charge of your
future model, the past, or your creative choice
right now?


The Task of Consciousness
To live consciously, you:
1. Define a future attractor that truly aligns
with what you desire.
2. Feel and embody that state now, allowing it
to reorganize your nervous system, thoughts,
and actions.
3. Act from that state, not from the inertia of
past conditioning.
Future states influence the present more than the
past because the future you hold in mind
determines the internal state and behaviors you
enact right now.
